 |
| [![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Crocodylidae_Distribution.png/250px-Crocodylidae_Distribution.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Crocodylidae_Distribution.png) |
| Global distribution of crocodile species |

A **crocodile** ([family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_\(biology\) "Family (biology)") **Crocodylidae**) or **true crocodile** is a large, [semiaquatic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiaquatic "Semiaquatic") [reptile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reptile "Reptile") that lives throughout the [tropics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropics "Tropics") in [Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Africa "Africa"), [Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Asia "Asia"), the [Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas "Americas") and [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia "Australia"). The term "crocodile" is sometimes used more loosely to include all [extant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extant_taxon "Extant taxon") members of the [order](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_\(biology\) "Order (biology)") [Crocodilia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodilia "Crocodilia"), which includes the [alligators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alligator "Alligator") and [caimans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caiman "Caiman") (both members of the family [Alligatoridae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alligatoridae "Alligatoridae")), the [gharial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gharial "Gharial") and [false gharial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/False_gharial "False gharial") (both members of the family [Gavialidae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gavialidae "Gavialidae")) as well as other extinct [taxa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxon "Taxon"). This article uses "crocodile" or "true crocodile" to refer only to the species [taxonomically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taxonomy_\(biology\) "Taxonomy (biology)") included in the Crocodylidae family, [extant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neontology#Extant_taxa_versus_extinct_taxa "Neontology") or [extinct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinct "Extinct").

Crocodile [size](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Measurement "Measurement"), [morphology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_\(biology\) "Morphology (biology)"), [behaviour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Behaviour "Behaviour") and [ecology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ecology "Ecology") differ among [species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species "Species"). However, they have many similarities in these areas as well. All crocodiles are [semiaquatic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semiaquatic "Semiaquatic") and tend to congregate in [freshwater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freshwater "Freshwater") habitats such as [rivers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/River "River"), [lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake "Lake"), [wetlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wetland "Wetland") and sometimes in [brackish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brackish "Brackish") water and [saltwater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seawater "Seawater"). They are [carnivorous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carnivorous "Carnivorous") animals, feeding mostly on [vertebrates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vertebrate "Vertebrate") such as [fish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fish "Fish"), [reptiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reptile "Reptile"), [birds](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bird "Bird") and [mammals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal "Mammal"), and sometimes on [invertebrates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Invertebrate "Invertebrate") such as [molluscs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mollusc "Mollusc") and [crustaceans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crustacean "Crustacean"), depending on [species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species "Species") and age. All crocodiles are [tropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical "Tropical") species that, unlike [alligators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alligator "Alligator"), are very sensitive to [cold](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold "Cold"). Many species are at the risk of [extinction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinction "Extinction"), some being classified as [critically endangered](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Critically_endangered "Critically endangered").

## Etymology

The word _crocodile_ (_croc._) was derived during the [Middle English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_English "Middle English") period[\[1\]](#cite_note-OED-1) from the [transliteration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transliteration "Transliteration") _krokódilos_ of a Greek[\[a\]](#cite_note-5) word which translates as "stones worm".[\[5\]](#cite_note-10.1093-6)[\[b\]](#cite_note-13) Through [Ancient Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greece "Ancient Greece")[\[12\]](#cite_note-14)[\[13\]](#cite_note-Несторов-15) the [English language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_language "English language") word has developed[\[5\]](#cite_note-10.1093-6) from Grecian origination in [Anatolia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anatolia#Ancient_Anatolia "Anatolia").[\[14\]](#cite_note-16)

A very early extant [Ancient Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancient_Greek "Ancient Greek") source is an [Aesop's Fable](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aesop%27s_Fable "Aesop's Fable") named [Ἀλώπηξ καὶ κροκόδειλος](https://el.wikipedia.org/wiki/s:%CE%91%CE%B9%CF%83%CF%8E%CF%80%CE%BF%CF%85_%CE%9C%CF%8D%CE%B8%CE%BF%CE%B9/%CE%91%CE%BB%CF%8E%CF%80%CE%B7%CE%BE_%CE%BA%CE%B1%CE%B9_%CE%BA%CF%81%CE%BF%CE%BA%CF%8C%CE%B4%CE%B5%CE%B9%CE%BB%CE%BF%CF%82 "el:s:Αισώπου Μύθοι/Αλώπηξ και κροκόδειλος") of the sixth century BC.[\[13\]](#cite_note-Несторов-15) [Herodotus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herodotus "Herodotus") a century after in consideration of the Greek word thought it was from the [Ionic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ionic_Greek "Ionic Greek") period.[\[15\]](#cite_note-17)

The [Latin language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin_language "Latin language") word _crocodilus_ existed in first century AD in the work _[Naturalis Historia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_Histories "Natural Histories")_ of [Pliny the Elder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder "Pliny the Elder").[\[16\]](#cite_note-18) Examples in writing in the sixth and seventh century AD, _crocodillorum_ and _crocodili_ existed,[\[13\]](#cite_note-Несторов-15) though _corcodrillus_ [\[17\]](#cite_note-pdf33468-19) and _cocodrillus_ [\[13\]](#cite_note-Несторов-15)[\[17\]](#cite_note-pdf33468-19) were forms in [Medieval Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin "Medieval Latin").[\[17\]](#cite_note-pdf33468-19) The Latin form is found as _cocodrille_ c. the 13th century in the [Old French](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Old_French "Old French") work [Li livres dou tresor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Li_livres_dou_tresor "Li livres dou tresor"), in which the croc. is _jaune_ (yellow).[\[18\]](#cite_note-20)

The earliest known source in the English language is within the work [Kyng Alisaunder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyng_Alisaunder "Kyng Alisaunder")[\[1\]](#cite_note-OED-1)[\[19\]](#cite_note-21) from towards the beginning of the 14th century, a [magical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Magic_\(supernatural\) "Magic (supernatural)") [romance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romance_\(prose_fiction\)#Medieval_romance "Romance (prose fiction)") poetry work of [rhyming couplets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhyming_couplets "Rhyming couplets"), where the word is found line 5720:[\[20\]](#cite_note-22)

Forth went the kyng wondres sekynde :

A griselich hest he gonne fynde;

So mychel seigh he neuere, ne non swiche;

Two heudes it had wel ferlich

To a cokedrill that on was liche,

That others the monoceros selcouthliche.[\[c\]](#cite_note-23)

Writing sometime after 1483 on his visit to the [Holy Lands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holy_Land "Holy Land") [Felix Fabri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Felix_Fabri "Felix Fabri") in German and Latin mentions the Cocodrillen and _cocodrillos_ respectively.[\[13\]](#cite_note-Несторов-15)[\[d\]](#cite_note-25) By 1538 the exact same form of the modern word as the current English is found in [French](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language#History "French language");[\[e\]](#cite_note-28)[\[24\]](#cite_note-29) _croc_. is within a poem of [Edmund Spenser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edmund_Spenser "Edmund Spenser"),[\[f\]](#cite_note-31)[\[25\]](#cite_note-EdSp-30) thought written in 1579–80,[\[26\]](#cite_note-32) and in the works of [William Shakespeare](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Shakespeare "William Shakespeare"), who died in 1616.[\[27\]](#cite_note-33) The similitude of the English word formation to a Latin source was caused at least by the transmission[\[28\]](#cite_note-34) of a relevant ancient science[\[29\]](#cite_note-35) from the influx of the publication of translations of Pliny the Elder some time towards the end of fourteenth and, or, beginning of fifteenth century. The publication of concrete realization in the anatomical work of [Andreas Vesalius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andreas_Vesalius "Andreas Vesalius") during 1543 inspired the creation of monographs and books of animals contributing to new science in [zoology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zoology "Zoology").[\[30\]](#cite_note-FEg.-36)

## Taxonomy and phylogeny

See also: [List of crocodilians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_crocodilians "List of crocodilians")

Crocodylidae was named as a [family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_\(biology\) "Family (biology)") by [Georges Cuvier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georges_Cuvier "Georges Cuvier") in 1807. It belongs to the larger [superfamily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superfamily_\(taxonomy\) "Superfamily (taxonomy)") [Crocodyloidea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodyloidea "Crocodyloidea"), which also includes additional extinct crocodile relatives. These all belong to the [order](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_\(biology\) "Order (biology)") [Crocodilia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodilia "Crocodilia"), which also includes [alligators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alligators "Alligators") and [gharials](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gharials "Gharials").

Although crocodiles, alligators, and the gharial are similar in appearance, they belong to separate [biological families](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_\(biology\) "Family (biology)"). The gharial, with its narrow [snout](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snout "Snout"), is easier to distinguish, while [morphological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_\(biology\) "Morphology (biology)") differences are more difficult to spot in crocodiles and alligators. The most obvious external differences are visible in the head, with crocodiles having narrower and longer heads, with a more V-shaped than a U-shaped snout compared to alligators and caimans. Another obvious trait is that the upper and lower jaws of the crocodiles are the same width, and the [teeth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Teeth "Teeth") in the lower jaw fall along the edge or outside the upper jaw when the mouth is closed; therefore, all teeth are visible, unlike an alligator, which possesses in the upper jaw small depressions into which the lower teeth fit. Also, when the crocodile's mouth is closed, the large fourth tooth in the lower jaw fits into a constriction in the upper jaw. For hard-to-distinguish specimens, the protruding tooth is the most reliable feature to define the [species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Species "Species")' [family](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Family_\(biology\) "Family (biology)").[\[31\]](#cite_note-37) Crocodiles have more [webbing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Webbing "Webbing") on the toes of the hind [feet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foot "Foot") and can better tolerate [saltwater](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saline_water "Saline water") due to specialized [salt glands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salt_gland "Salt gland") for filtering out salt, which are present, but non-functioning, in alligators. Another trait that separates crocodiles from other crocodilians is their much higher levels of [aggression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aggression "Aggression").[\[32\]](#cite_note-Guggisberg-38)

Crocodylidae is [cladistically](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cladistic "Cladistic") defined as a [crown group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crown_group "Crown group") composed of the [last common ancestor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Last_common_ancestor "Last common ancestor") of the [Nile crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nile_crocodile "Nile crocodile") (_Crocodylus niloticus_), the [Dwarf crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwarf_crocodile "Dwarf crocodile") (_Osteolaemus tetraspis_), and all of its descendants.[\[33\]](#cite_note-Rio2021-39) It contains two [subfamilies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subfamily_\(biology\) "Subfamily (biology)"): [Crocodylinae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylinae "Crocodylinae") and [Osteolaeminae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaeminae "Osteolaeminae").[\[34\]](#cite_note-Hekkala2021-40) Crocodylinae contains 13–14 living species, as well as 6 [extinct](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extinct "Extinct") species. Osteolaeminae was named by Christopher Brochu in 2003 as a subfamily of Crocodylidae separate from Crocodylinae,[\[35\]](#cite_note-C.thorbjarnarsoni-41) and contains the two [extant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extant_taxon "Extant taxon") [genera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Genus "Genus") _[Osteolaemus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaemus "Osteolaemus")_ and _[Mecistops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecistops "Mecistops")_, along with several extinct genera. The number of extant species within Osteolaeminae is currently in question.[\[36\]](#cite_note-Eaton-42)

-   **Subfamily [Crocodylinae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylinae "Crocodylinae")**
    -   Genus _[Crocodylus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus "Crocodylus")_
        -   _[Crocodylus acutus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_acutus "Crocodylus acutus")_, [American crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_crocodile "American crocodile")
        -   _[Crocodylus halli](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_halli "Crocodylus halli")_, [Hall's New Guinea crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hall%27s_New_Guinea_crocodile "Hall's New Guinea crocodile") found South of the [New Guinea Highlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Guinea_Highlands "New Guinea Highlands")[\[37\]](#cite_note-MurrayRussoZorrillaMcMahan2019-43)
        -   _[Crocodylus intermedius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_intermedius "Crocodylus intermedius")_, [Orinoco crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orinoco_crocodile "Orinoco crocodile")
        -   _[Crocodylus johnsoni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_johnsoni "Crocodylus johnsoni")_, [freshwater crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freshwater_crocodile "Freshwater crocodile"), or Johnstone's crocodile
        -   _[Crocodylus mindorensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_mindorensis "Crocodylus mindorensis")_, [Philippine crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippine_crocodile "Philippine crocodile")
        -   _[Crocodylus moreletii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_moreletii "Crocodylus moreletii")_, [Morelet's crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morelet%27s_crocodile "Morelet's crocodile") or Mexican crocodile
        -   _[Crocodylus niloticus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_niloticus "Crocodylus niloticus")_, [Nile crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nile_crocodile "Nile crocodile") or African crocodile (the subspecies found in Madagascar is sometimes called the black crocodile)
        -   _[Crocodylus novaeguineae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_novaeguineae "Crocodylus novaeguineae")_, [New Guinea crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Guinea_crocodile "New Guinea crocodile") found North of the [New Guinea Highlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Guinea_Highlands "New Guinea Highlands")
            -   _[Crocodylus raninus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_raninus "Crocodylus raninus")_, the [Borneo crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Borneo_crocodile "Borneo crocodile"), is related to _C. novaeguineae_, but whether or not it is a distinct species remains unclear.[\[38\]](#cite_note-Ross1990-44)
        -   _[Crocodylus palustris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_palustris "Crocodylus palustris")_, [mugger](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mugger_Crocodile "Mugger Crocodile"), marsh or Indian crocodile
        -   _[Crocodylus porosus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_porosus "Crocodylus porosus")_, [saltwater crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saltwater_crocodile "Saltwater crocodile") or estuarine crocodile
        -   _[Crocodylus rhombifer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_rhombifer "Crocodylus rhombifer")_, [Cuban crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuban_crocodile "Cuban crocodile")
        -   _[Crocodylus siamensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_siamensis "Crocodylus siamensis")_, [Siamese crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siamese_crocodile "Siamese crocodile") (may be extinct in the wild)
        -   _[Crocodylus suchus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_suchus "Crocodylus suchus")_, [West African crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_African_crocodile "West African crocodile"), desert or sacred crocodile
        -   _[Crocodylus anthropophagus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_anthropophagus "Crocodylus anthropophagus")_†
        -   _[Crocodylus checchiai](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_checchiai "Crocodylus checchiai")_†
        -   _[Crocodylus falconensis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_falconensis "Crocodylus falconensis")_†
        -   _[Crocodylus palaeindicus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_palaeindicus "Crocodylus palaeindicus")_†
        -   _[Crocodylus thorbjarnarsoni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus_thorbjarnarsoni "Crocodylus thorbjarnarsoni")_†
    -   Genus _[Voay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voay "Voay")_†
        -   _[Voay robustus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voay_robustus "Voay robustus")_† (formerly _Crocodylus robustus_)
-   **Subfamily [Osteolaeminae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaeminae "Osteolaeminae")**
    -   Genus _[Osteolaemus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaemus "Osteolaemus")_
        -   _[Osteolaemus tetraspis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaemus_tetraspis "Osteolaemus tetraspis")_, [dwarf crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dwarf_crocodile "Dwarf crocodile")
        -   _[Osteolaemus osborni](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaemus_osborni "Osteolaemus osborni")_, [Osborn's dwarf crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osborn%27s_dwarf_crocodile "Osborn's dwarf crocodile")
        -   Recent (2009) DNA analysis indicate a third distinct species, currently unnamed.[\[36\]](#cite_note-Eaton-42)
    -   Genus _[Mecistops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecistops "Mecistops")_
        -   _[Mecistops cataphractus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecistops_cataphractus "Mecistops cataphractus")_ [West African slender-snouted crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_African_slender-snouted_crocodile "West African slender-snouted crocodile")
        -   _[Mecistops leptorhynchus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecistops_leptorhynchus "Mecistops leptorhynchus")_ [Central African slender-snouted crocodile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_African_slender-snouted_crocodile "Central African slender-snouted crocodile")
    -   Genus _[Brochuchus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brochuchus "Brochuchus")_†
        -   _[Brochuchus pigotti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brochuchus_pigotti "Brochuchus pigotti")_† (formerly _Crocodylus pigotti_)
        -   _[Brochuchus parvidens](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brochuchus_parvidens "Brochuchus parvidens")_†
    -   Genus _[Euthecodon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euthecodon "Euthecodon")_†
        -   _[Euthecodon nitriae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euthecodon_nitriae "Euthecodon nitriae")_†
        -   _[Euthecodon brumpti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euthecodon_brumpti "Euthecodon brumpti")_†
        -   _[Euthecodon arambourgi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Euthecodon_arambourgi "Euthecodon arambourgi")_†
    -   Genus _[Rimasuchus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rimasuchus "Rimasuchus")_†
        -   _[Rimasuchus lloydi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rimasuchus_lloydi "Rimasuchus lloydi")_† (formerly _Crocodylus lloydi_)

### Phylogeny

Recent molecular studies using [DNA sequencing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DNA_sequencing "DNA sequencing") have shown crocodiles to be more closely related to the [gavialids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gavialid "Gavialid") rather than to [alligators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alligator "Alligator"), contrary to prior theories based on [morphological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_\(biology\) "Morphology (biology)") studies alone.[\[39\]](#cite_note-45)[\[40\]](#cite_note-Gatesy2008-46)[\[41\]](#cite_note-bite-47)[\[42\]](#cite_note-LeeYates2018-48)[\[34\]](#cite_note-Hekkala2021-40)

Below is a [cladogram](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cladogram "Cladogram") showing the relationships of the major [extant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extant_taxon "Extant taxon") crocodile groups based on molecular studies, excluding separate extinct taxa:

Below is a more detailed cladogram of Crocodylidae, based on a 2021 study using [paleogenomics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleogenomics "Paleogenomics") that extracted DNA from the extinct _[Voay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voay "Voay")_.[\[34\]](#cite_note-Hekkala2021-40) Recently recognised species (_M. leptorhynchus_, _C. halli_ and the third _Osteolaemus_ species) placed according to 2023 study by Sales-Oliveira _et al._[\[43\]](#cite_note-Sales-Oliveira2023-49)

Alternatively, some [morphological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morphology_\(biology\) "Morphology (biology)") studies have recovered _[Mecistops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecistops "Mecistops")_ as a [basal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basal_\(phylogeny\) "Basal (phylogeny)") member of [Crocodylinae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylinae "Crocodylinae"), more closely related to _[Crocodylus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crocodylus "Crocodylus")_ than to _[Osteolaemus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaemus "Osteolaemus")_ and the other members of [Osteolaeminae](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Osteolaeminae "Osteolaeminae"),[\[33\]](#cite_note-Rio2021-39)[\[44\]](#cite_note-Azzara2021-50) as shown in the cladogram below.[\[44\]](#cite_note-Azzara2021-50)
